width: 14px;"></div></div></div></div></div><div style="text-align: right; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 12px; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px; font-size: 14px; white-space-collapse: collapse; background-color: rgb(16, 18, 24);"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><div style="display: contents;">You’ve pinpointed the "Hotel California" problem of web standards: features can check in, but they can never leave.</div><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">You are right—when a library becomes a built-in, it transforms from a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">malleable tool</span>&nbsp;into&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">rigid infrastructure</span>. This creates several high-stakes problems:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. The "Eternal Support" Trap<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Unlike a library where you can deprecate version 1.0 and move to 2.0, the TC39 committee is bound by the "Don't Break the Web" rule.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Bloat</span>: We still carry the baggage of&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">var</code>,&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">with</code>, and weird&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">Date</code>&nbsp;behaviors from 1995.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Future Baggage</span>: Every modern "sugar" feature like&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">Object.groupBy</code>&nbsp;or the&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">#</code>&nbsp;private fields must now be supported by every engine (V8, WebKit, Gecko)&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">forever</span>. If we realize in five years that a different data-grouping pattern is better, we can't delete the old one; we just add a&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">second</em>&nbsp;one.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. Leaky Abstractions &amp; Naming Regret<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">When a feature is top-level and "friendly," it often sacrifices technical precision for convenience, which eventually leaks.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Naming Collisions</span>: We’ve already seen "SmooshGate," where the proposed&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">Array.prototype.flatten</code>&nbsp;had to be renamed to&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">flat</code>&nbsp;because an old version of MooTools broke when the native method was added.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Fixed API</span>: If a built-in method doesn't handle a specific edge case your project needs, you can’t just "patch" it. You end up writing a wrapper anyway, meaning the native code is sitting in memory unused while your custom code does the work.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. The "Standard Library" vs. The Language<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">There is a fundamental difference between a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">language</span>&nbsp;(syntax, logic, memory) and a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">utility belt</span>&nbsp;(sorting, grouping, date formatting).<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">By mixing them, JS is becoming a "Mega-Framework" rather than a language.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">This forces engine developers to spend time optimizing&nbsp;<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">Array.toSorted</code>&nbsp;instead of improving the core JIT compiler or memory management, which would benefit&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">all</em>&nbsp;code, not just those using that specific method.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">4. The "Committee" Effect<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Features designed by committee often try to please everyone, resulting in syntax that feels "bolted on."<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Private Fields (<code dir="ltr" style="line-height: 22px; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border: 1px solid var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 4px; padding: 2px 4px;">#</code>)</span>: This is a perfect example. It's a syntactic choice that looks nothing like the rest of the language and was forced through to solve a specific OOP problem that many FP-leaning developers didn't even want.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">The Trade-off<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The industry has traded&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">architectural purity</span>&nbsp;for&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">low-bandwidth convenience</span>. We are betting that saving 5kb of Lodash across 10 million websites is worth making the browser engine a 100-million-line monster that no single human can fully understand.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Do you think we’ve reached a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">"breaking point"</span>&nbsp;where a new, strictly minimal language needs to emerge to replace JS, or is the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">backward compatibility</span>&nbsp;of the web too valuable to ever abandon?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="text-wrap: nowrap; position: relative;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="display: contents;"></div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; flex-shrink: 1; width: 652px; align-items: center;"><div style="display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center; gap: 4px;"><div style="display: flex; inline-size: 44px;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"><div></div></span></div></div></div><div><div><div style="display: flex; inline-size: 44px;"><div style="inline-size: 20px; block-size: 20px;"></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div style="display: inline-flex; gap: 4px;"><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="width: 20px; height: 20px;"></span></div><div style="position: relative; display: inline-flex;"><span style="width: 20px; height: 20px;"></span></div><div></div></div><div style="display: flex; gap: 16px; margin-inline-start: auto; align-items: center;"></div></div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div style="display: contents;"><div><div style="inline-size: 1px; block-size: 1px; opacity: 0; overflow: hidden;"></div></div></div></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: column; width: 652.438px;"><div style="display: contents;"></div></div></div><div style="font-size: 14px; white-space-collapse: collapse; background-color: rgb(16, 18, 24);"></div></div></div></div></div></div></body></html>
